    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

And Elias </span>
  <span id="freeText14388680167534017687" style="display:none">Elias and Laia are running for their lives. After the events of the Fourth Trial, Martial soldiers hunt the two fugitives as they flee the city of Serra and undertake a perilous journey through the heart of the Empire.<br /><br />Laia is determined to break into Kauf—the Empire’s most secure and dangerous prison—to save her brother, who is the key to the Scholars’ survival. And Elias is determined to help Laia succeed, even if it means giving up his last chance at freedom.<br /><br />But dark forces, human and otherworldly, work against Laia and Elias. The pair must fight every step of the way to outsmart their enemies: the bloodthirsty Emperor Marcus, the merciless Commandant, the sadistic Warden of Kauf, and, most heartbreaking of all, Helene—Elias’s former friend and the Empire’s newest Blood Shrike.<br /><br />Bound to Marcus’s will, Helene faces a torturous mission of her own—one that might destroy her: find the traitor Elias Veturius and the Scholar slave who helped him escape…and kill them both.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">According to the author, the mask just covers half the face and it wraps around the back in a shape of a claw. I thought it was the whole face too but<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">According to the author, the mask just covers half the face and it wraps around the back in a shape of a claw. I thought it was the whole face too but that's what she said so... its her book so I guess half mask then. *Here is where i got this information: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.hypable.com/ember-in-the-ashes-sequel-movie/">http://www.hypable.com/ember-in-the-a...</a><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_933').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1416031602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416031602" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416031602?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416031602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3857240586150140391"><blockquote>
  <i>I realize I am not staring into his eyes. I am staring into my future.<br/>I see it for a moment. Pain. Suffering. Horror. All that I love, all that matters to me, awash in blood.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Oh my god. I loved it.</b><br/><br/>Last year, I read and enjoyed an advance copy of an unknown book from a debut author - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_' title='An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Ember in the Ashes</a>. I sped through it, loved it, rated it five stars, and thought that was the end of that. On to the next one. Like most books I rate and review, I expected it to be forgotten in a sea of YA. B</span>
  <span id="freeText3857240586150140391" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I realize I am not staring into his eyes. I am staring into my future.<br />I see it for a moment. Pain. Suffering. Horror. All that I love, all that matters to me, awash in blood.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Oh my god. I loved it.</b><br /><br />Last year, I read and enjoyed an advance copy of an unknown book from a debut author - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>. I sped through it, loved it, rated it five stars, and thought that was the end of that. On to the next one. Like most books I rate and review, I expected it to be forgotten in a sea of YA. But suddenly, out of nowhere, it was a bestseller! And that's when I got some unprecedented backlash for my review.<br /><br /><i>“I’m really surprised you liked this.”<br />“This is just like ten million other books - how can you think it's so good?”<br />“I’m not sure I can take your opinion seriously anymore.”</i><br /><br /><b>Ouch.</b><br /><br />And I was like:<br /><i>“What? I just liked it.”</i><br /> *voice getting smaller*<br /><i>"I’m not saying it’s the best book ever or anything.”</i><br />*even smaller*<br /><i>“Okay, maybe it wasn’t that great.”</i><br /><br />But, you know what? <b>Fuck it</b>. I loved this book and the first one. I know they’re not something out of this world and I know the story is not that original, but I don’t care. Because, for me, it’s not what a book is about, but <b>how it’s told</b>. And I think both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> are told with <b>nail-biting tension</b> and <b>perfectly-paced action</b>. I hung on the author’s every word.<br /><br />I honestly don't give a shit anymore if these books are <i>objectively good</i> (what even is that, anyway?). I race through them. My heart pounds. The pages just fly by in my desperation to find out what happens. They're nasty and brutal, full of evil surprises and even more evil things that you see coming but can't stop.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> picks up right where we left off and, if you enjoyed the first one, it's very easy to be pulled back into the rhythm of the story and world without recapping. I wondered if I would be able to easily follow the stories of Laia, Elias and Helene after more than a year away from them, but I needn't have worried. I felt the rush of everything coming back to me as I was once again immersed in this world.<br /><br />Often, sequels wander aimlessly, but this one was <b>perfectly plotted</b>. It didn't feel like it was bridging a gap - the story moves along, many important and awful things happen, secrets are revealed and Tahir rounds off this installment well, whilst still promising so much more from the next book. I can't freaking wait.<br /><br />I love all three narrators, but Helene is worth five stars alone. Out of all of them, she has been through the worst kind of hell and has had to make the most difficult decisions. I love her internal conflicts over what she wants to do and what she should do. She's sharp and smart, just cool enough to be badass, whilst also painfully, relatably human.<br /><br />Seriously, I just have nothing bad to say about this book. I think, if I tried, I could feasibly come up with an original-ish idea for a fantasy that has not been done before. However, I think to take a somewhat familiar story and inject it with new life so that it becomes virtually unputdownable is a much more commendable achievement. Bravo, Ms Tahir, bravo.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3857240586150140391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1736976393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736976393" />
    <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess"><img alt="The Burning Rose (Jess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605317941p2/48477217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736976393?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Burning Rose (Jess)" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess">The Burning Rose (Jess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736976393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12746361785064845601">5/5 stars. I want to cry! <br/>How do you understand that the book you just finished reading is a good book? Which is worth 5 whole stars, and maybe even more?<br/>I'll tell you my opinion - you should feel it. You have to feel the characters, go through the experience they are going through. You have to feel that you are experiencing what is going on in the book with the characters.<br/>It's a very great connection to a book, and it doesn't happen with most books. Usually, you just read the book from your poi</span>
  <span id="freeText12746361785064845601" style="display:none">5/5 stars. I want to cry! <br />How do you understand that the book you just finished reading is a good book? Which is worth 5 whole stars, and maybe even more?<br />I'll tell you my opinion - you should feel it. You have to feel the characters, go through the experience they are going through. You have to feel that you are experiencing what is going on in the book with the characters.<br />It's a very great connection to a book, and it doesn't happen with most books. Usually, you just read the book from your point of view as a reader. It's hard for you to connect with the characters. And, if you did connect with a particular character, that doesn't mean you necessarily feel and become the character.<br />If you don't understand what the hell I'm talking about -because I'm a completely complicated person who can't explain herself- I'll explain now.<br /><br />From the first book I connected with Elias.<br />Yes yes, Elias. Not Laia. I know many of you have mostly connected to Laia, I don't, but I'll go into that later.<br />Me and Elias are alike. I will not begin to explain why, because it’ll be long, but our personality is similar.<br />Throughout the first book, the moment I was sucked into the plot, I could put myself in the position of Elias. I experienced the emotions with him, I experienced the failures with him. It was amazing. It doesn't happen to me with characters usually, so it's a delightful feeling in my opinion. It's fun.<br />As soon as I started reading the current book, I was worried that this connection would pass. It happened to me before that I became very attached to a certain character, but in the next book she/he changed a bit, and the connection broke off. So it didn't happen in this book. I could still feel Elias. Experience the world he‘s in. But thank God this connection isn’t physical, is it? It could’ve been sucks. (those who don't know what I'm talking about - sorry, don't do spoilers).<br />So in summary: Elias is a freaking king.<br /><br />Now let's talk about Laia.<br />Like I said before, I'm not a big fan of Laia. And to be honest? I liked her even more in the first book. In the current book she was a little far from me. Don't get me wrong, she's a good character. But I guess it's because of my amazing connection to Elias and the fact that Tahir added Helene's point of view.<br /><br />Oh, Helene. We will talk about her, I have many things to say about her.<br />In the first book, she confused me. Big Time. In one episode I thought she was nice, in another I thought she was annoying, in another I said to myself "Oh! What a badass!”, And, in another chapter, I thought to myself, "What the hell?". So yeah, I couldn't even form an opinion about her. Which is why I am so happy that Tahir decided to add her point of view.<br />From the first episode, which was told from Helene's point of view, I could begin to piece together the puzzle pieces of her character. I could finally understand her, accept her and then love her.<br />And yes, I might surprise you again, but I love Helene more than Laia. (And like I said, that's probably the reason for my distancing from Laia's character, too).<br /><br />Is it just me or is this review very confused? You see, it took me 4 days to write it. I don't know, I feel like I'm confusing everything, maybe it's just me, but I always find it hard to explain myself when I talk about something so good.<br /><br />So characters, characters, characters...<br />I have to take a few lines and write about Tas, this sweet, strong boy I loved so much. And Darin, who I finally got to know. Although that’s obviously not enough, and I must pick up the third book. And Helene's amazing family. And IZZI, oh IZZI!<br />And Keenan, who I love so much. Really, even after this book, after all the craziness that was discovered, I still really loved Keenan's character.<br />And you can't forget Harper, of course. He was so intrigued to me! His character was so intriguing. I felt like I was slowly sipping from the bottle, and I hadn't even reached half of it. I really liked him, and I look forward to getting to know him better in the next book.<br /><br />So after talking about the characters, I'll talk about the plot.<br />Sabaa Thair knows how to write a good book. She knows how to keep the reader in suspense and make him turn a page and keep reading.<br />It's amazing how you always stay thirsty for more, how you can't put the book out of your hands. How you keep expecting something and still enjoy it when you receive it.<br />I'm not sure I'll be able to get more opinions into this review, because I'm starting to feel that my excited brain is starting to confuse everything again.. So I'll stop here.<br />Excuse me if you read this shit called "review" and I hope you enjoyed this book as much as I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12746361785064845601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1318721557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318721557" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1318721557?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=huge-character-development">huge-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=shocking-betrayals">shocking-betrayals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=dark-atmosphere">dark-atmosphere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=swoon-worthy-characters">swoon-worthy-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=good-vs-bad">good-vs-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=holy-shit">holy-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1318721557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6469277697693588094"><i>
  <b>“So long as you fight the darkness, you stand in the light.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>A Torch Against the Night</i> is the very glorious sequel I had expected from Sabaa Tahir. But what distinguishes itself from its prequel is the <b>otherworldliness</b> of it. The breath of Death on our characters' necks. The villain(s) that are evil incarnate. The idea of a prescribed destiny. The new abilities and powers. The demons, the stories, the souls -- everything combines with a well-built plot, an expanded universe and realistic, fla</span>
  <span id="freeText6469277697693588094" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“So long as you fight the darkness, you stand in the light.”</b>
</i><br><br><i>A Torch Against the Night</i> is the very glorious sequel I had expected from Sabaa Tahir. But what distinguishes itself from its prequel is the <b>otherworldliness</b> of it. The breath of Death on our characters' necks. The villain(s) that are evil incarnate. The idea of a prescribed destiny. The new abilities and powers. The demons, the stories, the souls -- everything combines with a well-built plot, an expanded universe and realistic, flawed portrayals of characters in order to deliver the best kind of chills. <br><br>From the very first page, we're thrust back into Tahir's fictional world quite violently. Starting exactly where Ember ended, we're reminded of the stakes, the world and the unnatural. Plus Elias and Laia's slow burn, sizzling chemistry. <br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-MV8DrXOWTlQ/V8rfhx9fCfI/AAAAAAAAQaU/pnfQZV6Og9IxlxBYCT1zcYaCze8WeoapACLcB/s1600/52fbd354291899329376c0a41c440306.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472913309i/20354212.jpg" width="279" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I had initially rated this book with 5 stars, but I ended up changing it because no matter how much I loved how it all unfolded, I had to admit there was something irking me: the inconsistency of the pace. The plot unravels with several ramifications that, at first glance, only deter from the main storyline. Or at least the one I deemed main in my head. Raider's Roost. Nur. The Waiting Place. All the back and forth between Antium and the countryside. But they did enrich a captivating world, so I partly appreciated it. However, I still found myself wishing more exciting things happened. And I can guarantee that's what is probably going to happen in the third novel, because wheels have been finally been put into motion. <br><br>Regardless, there is a sort of redundancy in both Elias and Helene's POVs as they both battle their own demons. Which is the only flaw of this book, in my opinion. <br><br>If you had any inkling of love for Elias in the first book, then prepare yourself for full-on worship and adoration. This sequel painted him in true hero colors, highlighting his altruism, his devotion, his intensity and, most of all, his fairness. There was a particular character development that broke my heart which I hope somehow will be reversed by the end of the series because from the beginning I had the image of Elias and Laia as Emperor and Empress stuck on my retina, with Helene as Blood Shrike. I also need to mention his amazing dynamic with his adoptive family which was a wonder to see. SO BEAUTIFUL. <br><br>This time around, Laia makes a lot of mistakes. Disastrous one after disastrous one. But I liked that instead of drowning in guilt, she turned a critical eye against her actions and learned from them. Betrayals change her. New allies shape her. And love strengthens her. <br><br><a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-QRDeRszH0Es/V8rfhzZ0V-I/AAAAAAAAQaY/1vb7X-mrHzgRfKxwEU3QqHtlqEcjLSm6ACLcB/s1600/ember-laia.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="246" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472913327i/20354216.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“It takes only a split second for life to go horribly wrong. To fix the mess, I need a thousand things to go right. The distance from one bit of luck to the next feels as great as the distance across oceans. But, I decide in this moment, I will bridge that distance, again and again, until I win. I will not fail.”</b>
</i><br><br>Helene Aquilla, however, was incredible. I didn't think it was possible to love her more than I did in Ember, but I was so wrong. She grows a lot in this installment, through emotional hardships that plague her at every step. Her whole journey is a turning point, the stepping stone for her maturity. The question of duty vs. heart remains deeply rooted into her persona and heartbreak shapes her anew in an astounding, almost terrifying image. I cannot wait to see how this colder, broken, hollowed Helene is going to enact her revenge and show the world her wrath. After all, the title of this book is an omen to the fire in Helene Aquilla. <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-nf2knNFIX7A/V8reJsSNa2I/AAAAAAAAQZ8/yajchE3h8ZAvSoR7B8ajzwvY13eISsLIwCLcB/s1600/4612c56132dc99f3806f00f95c0f4be5.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472913102i/20354043.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“But you, Helene Aquilla, are no swift-burning spark. You are a torch against the night - if you dare to let yourself burn.” </b>
</i><br><br>The matter of the 'love-square' as I like to call it is entirely resolved by the end of the novel. At least I think so. Or just let's go ahead and call it a pseudo-love-triangle because even though the focus is on an almost-pair that has my heart bursting with joy, the possibility of old flames coming to life yet again is not wholly crushed because feelings of mutual love still reside in a back corner, even though they are one of deep friendship. But the romance situation resolves messily and I was displeased (or better yet, uncertain) of how the story developed on a couple of occasions.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Failure doesn’t define you. It’s what you do after you fail that determines whether you are a leader or a waste of perfectly good air.”</b>
</i> <br><br>By far, the most compelling aspects of this continuation are the villains. The Commandant manages to upgrade her bitch title to the one of ultimate bitch. I swear, I haven't read such a beautifully written bad character in a long time, one that thrives on power and bloodshed, on gore and brutality and perennial violence. It was fascinating and utterly horrifying to witness how easily she can make a whole nation crumble. <br><br>The Warden is a new bad guy but immensely intriguing in his sadistic ways. The Nightbringer establishes himself as a layered, complex character that is not as straightforward as one might think. Honestly, I do not know what to further expect from him because his involvement in this book is jaw-dropping. <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ilzAq_gvNq8/V8reJju90xI/AAAAAAAAQaA/brQToSd4XSQR_vERJWgDsciQ6pE8eWkdACLcB/s1600/a72c562b8692f4418a5292d2fc1deaac.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472913102i/20354044.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Another one of the most intriguing characters of the whole book is Marcus. I loved his cunningness and his... cleverness, I suppose, even if he's not one of the good guys. It was one of those instances where you can just clap to the performance, but be glad he's just fictional. <br><br>Other things worth mentioning: the Aquilla family; <i>Avitas Harper</i> (omg you're gonna love him and I hope he plays a bigger part in the following books); <b>KEENAN HOLY SHIT KEENAN;</b> Izzzzzzyyyyyy; COOK; Shaeva (oh, sweetie); Afya, the most badass and honorable Zaldara ever; <b>Elias with children around -- you're not up to it, I'm telling you.</b><br><br>The wait until 2018 will be a torturous one, because <i>A Torch Against the Night</i> moved all the right pieces to make my heart crack and crave more destruction. Thrilling, captivating and intelligently written, this sequel cemented the status of this series as a 'MUST-READ' so I urge you to read it the first chance you've got. <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3 </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6469277697693588094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1416018238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416018238" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416018238?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416018238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2570960503106441790"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best YA fantasy & science fiction category 2016!</b><br/><br/><i>"Force won't work," Harper murmurs. "You need to outwit them. You need secrets."<br/><br/>"Secrets are a snake's way of doing business."<br/><br/>"And snakes survive."</i><br/><br/>i didn't love this as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_' title='An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Ember in the Ashes</a>, but it's a seriously fun book regardless. the problem is that the first one was <i>so</i> strong, it's a tough act to follow. this one is certainly not lacking in action or worldbuilding or interesting characters - </span>
  <span id="freeText2570960503106441790" style="display:none"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best YA fantasy &amp; science fiction category 2016!</b><br><br><i>"Force won't work," Harper murmurs. "You need to outwit them. You need secrets."<br><br>"Secrets are a snake's way of doing business."<br><br>"And snakes survive."</i><br><br>i didn't love this as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>, but it's a seriously fun book regardless. the problem is that the first one was <i>so</i> strong, it's a tough act to follow. this one is certainly not lacking in action or worldbuilding or interesting characters - there's plenty for them to do, and the stakes are sky-high, but it just didn't seem as well-constructed as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>. there's a rushed quality to the plotting here - many instances where it comes across like a breathless, "we need to do this oh now we are doing it, good!" which is great for the book's pacing - this is a fast, fast read - but it feels like too much was glossed-over and sacrificed to that pacing.<br><br>but whatever - it's a minor quibble that irritated me when i was reading it, but when i think back on all the stuff that happened in this book, my irritation is totally squashed by my much stronger feelings of having read something fun and dark and fierce.<br><br>all the great characters are back - laia, elias, the commandant, marcus, keenan, and helene. heleeeeeeene. who is here given all the space she needs to be the powerful, complicated, thoughtful, badass, pragmatic creature we got glimpses of in the first book. here, in her new role as blood shrike - the sword that does the ruthless emperor's will, she really shines. <br><br>speaking of shining - the scene revealing the origin of this book's name?? CHILLS! <br><br>helene is my new favorite character in all things.<br><br><i>I'm Blood Shrike. It is time to show my strength.</i><br><br>as far as the other characters go - tahir does a great job clipping elias' wings a bit here. it's almost unfair to have a character who is unmatched in fighting prowess - it takes the elements of danger and tension away from any action scenes. but she came up with a really great, fair way to level the playing field in order to increase the peril of our characters, and the things that change for elias over the course of the book (no spoilers here!) are both dramatically interesting and textually appropriate. not what i would have guessed, but very satisfying.<br><br>and laia - i dunno, she's not my favorite heroine of all time. there's a lot i respect about her character, but i like my heroines to have a little more of an edge to them, and laia's just a bit too squeaky for me, and her very formal avoidance of contractions grates on me a bit. don't get me wrong, i feel for her when bad things happen, and that closing scene was affecting, but what can i say - i'm team helene and i'm a one-woman gal.<br><br>all the magical bits from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> - the parts that i was so frustrated about not getting explanations for when i learned it was conceived as a standalone, are fully defined here, and they add an extra layer of intrigue to what was already a pretty kickass world. <br><br>it's a rough ride - there's a lot of blood, a lot of horrific casualties of revolution and ambition, a lot of sacrifice for the good of the empire:<br><br><i>The Empire must come first - above your desires, your friendships, your wants.</i><br><br>it's all wonderful, horrific, consequence-bleeding stuff. and there had better be a third book coming, because i want some vengeance - righteous, splattery vengeance.<br><br>gimmie.<br><br>*****************************************<br><br>oh, YAY! i was deemed cool enough to snag an arc of this after all! and while i was not in the top-tier of cool kids who got the accompanying power bracelet:<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469480183i/19822827._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>if you have a glue gun, a toilet paper roll and some glitter, that's easy enough to remedy. behold!<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_4939_zpsnlsklfvl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469480659i/19823009._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_4939_zpsnlsklfvl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_4944_zpsu6mnguvf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469480659i/19823008._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_4944_zpsu6mnguvf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1875483130" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875483130" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875483130?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875483130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5204254898357969131">This is Helene’s book.<br/><br/>Well not quite, but she plays such a grander role than she did in the first book. In fact, she annoyed me to no end in the latter, but in this sequel we learn more about her and are shown different facets of her personality.<br/><br/>The fact that her family is in danger is not a positive thing, but somehow it made Helene look more humane to my eyes. She isn’t the rigid, rule-abider soldier I saw her as before being witness to her softer, vulnerable side anymore.<br/><br/>There’s much running </span>
  <span id="freeText5204254898357969131" style="display:none">This is Helene’s book.<br /><br />Well not quite, but she plays such a grander role than she did in the first book. In fact, she annoyed me to no end in the latter, but in this sequel we learn more about her and are shown different facets of her personality.<br /><br />The fact that her family is in danger is not a positive thing, but somehow it made Helene look more humane to my eyes. She isn’t the rigid, rule-abider soldier I saw her as before being witness to her softer, vulnerable side anymore.<br /><br />There’s much running around in this. It’s no wonder we see Laia and Elias running for their lives on the cover. It’s a lot of moving around, falling into traps and then getting out of them. Elias and Laia want to free Darin from prison, so most of the story centers on them trying to reach the prison.<br /><br />But then there’s Helene who is assigned to capture Elias alive. You may think, lucky her, she finally has the status she most likely dreamed of all her life and hundreds of soldiers ready to follow her anywhere, but it’s not so easy. She does, after all, as we know, love Elias. Or not?<br /><br />Sabaa Tahir writes so, so well. If any other author had written this book, chances are I would have given up on it after the first couple of chapters, because it’s very, very slow and filled with dialog that could easily have been cut or exchanged for some action scenes. But because Sabaa Tahir wrote this, I had no choice but to finish it.<br /><br />This series is not one that doesn’t take itself seriously. It’s not silly or unfathomable. The way Sabaa Tahir writes makes everything seem probable, like these characters could truly be alive in an alternative, magical universe. At first, I was befuddled by the inclusion of magical abilities, because it’s not as if the world-building needs them, but they sure come in handy and I’m eager to see how they will develop within the characters. <br /><br />I sure do wish it were faster paced, but otherwise, A TORCH AGAINST THE NIGHT is flawlessly-written and extremely intricate. <br /><br />PS. Was anyone else reminded of the video game ‘‘Rise of the Tomb Raider’’ featuring the unique Lara Croft when they read this?<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5204254898357969131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1643930263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643930263" />
    <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books"><img alt="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464902542p2/372001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books">Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=2016-release">2016-release</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643930263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2719545269697269418">This review can also be found <a href='http://danaandthebooks.com/2016/10/25/atatn/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>on my blog, Dana and the Books</a>.<br/><br/><a href='http://danaandthebooks.com/2016/05/27/review-an-ember-in-the-ashes/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><em>An Ember in the Ashes</em> was one of my favourite books</a> from the past few years so it's only natural that I counted down the days to the sequel. In fact, I found out my local book shop had it stocked a couple days before the UK release date, so I frantically ran over and recruited the bookseller to help me find it. Poor guy must have thought I was insane - I don't think I even brushed my hair I was so desperate to get my hands on it. Well,</span>
  <span id="freeText2719545269697269418" style="display:none">This review can also be found <a href="http://danaandthebooks.com/2016/10/25/atatn/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog, Dana and the Books</a>.<br><br><a href="http://danaandthebooks.com/2016/05/27/review-an-ember-in-the-ashes/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><em>An Ember in the Ashes</em> was one of my favourite books</a> from the past few years so it's only natural that I counted down the days to the sequel. In fact, I found out my local book shop had it stocked a couple days before the UK release date, so I frantically ran over and recruited the bookseller to help me find it. Poor guy must have thought I was insane - I don't think I even brushed my hair I was so desperate to get my hands on it. Well, that wonderful man found the ONLY copy they received and IT WAS MINE.<br><br>For some reason I cannot possibly fathom, the UK edition doesn't include a map.<br><br>WHY?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477415279ra/20949836.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://siobhansnovelties.wordpress.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Siobhan</a> was lovely and sent me bunch of photos of her map-abundant Canadian edition and I am forever in her debt.<br><br>I was so eager to continue Elias and Laia's journey I started reading straight away. Surprisingly, the first 100 or so pages didn't excite me the way <em>Embers</em> did. I started to get a bit worried. Would this sequel pale in comparison to such a strong debut?<br><br>BUT, after I passed the 150 page mark and got over the map snubbing I got that same thrill I did when reading <em>Embers</em>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477415279ra/20949837.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We got some pretty awesome fight scenes and great character development.<br><br>And then...<br><br>AND THEN we got the mother of all MOTHER FUCKING PLOT TWISTS.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477415279ra/20949838.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, it probably wasn't as shocking as I'm making it out to be but I never pick up on hints or foreshadowing so I was legitimately shocked.<br><br>My actual face:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477415279ra/20949839.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While I think <em>An Ember in the Ashes</em> is the stronger novel overall, <em>A Torch Against the Night</em> was still a fantastic follow up. I can't wait until the third one (2018?!?!).<br><br>Sabaa Tahir, I bow down to you and your wonderfulness.<br><br><strong>This was a buddy review with Siobhan - <a href="https://siobhansnovelties.wordpress.com/2016/10/25/joint-review-a-torch-against-the-night/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">don't forget to check out her awesome review!</a></strong><br><br>(<a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/Torch-Against-the-Night-Saba-Tahir/9780008160340/?a_aid=DanaAndTheBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2eI9IV0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US </a>/ <a href="http://amzn.to/2ertu92" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon Canada</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2eG5zSC" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>)<br></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698326801" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36179502-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507346345p2/36179502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698326801?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/36179502-rose">Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179502-rose?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179502-rose?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179502-rose?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179502-rose?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698326801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6475890118942487496"><blockquote>
<b>S A B A A <br/>T A H I R<br/>R U I N E D<br/>M E.</b><br/><br/><b>Side effects if reading ATATN:</b> dizziness, fatigue, lightheadedness, clammy skin, cold sweat, <i>P A I N.</i> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468921972ra/19758523.gif' width='auto' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>If you’ve read any of my updates, you’d know how <i>terrified</i> I was going into this- that I was expecting the worst.. and now I’m just sorry that I even doubted Sabaa Tahir. Because<b> absolutely every part of this book was brutal</b>, but also <i>perfection</i>. <br/><br/>All the best parts of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_' title='An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Ember in the Ashes</a> were still a part of this story; the <i>complexity </i>of each and every chara</span>
  <span id="freeText6475890118942487496" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<b>S A B A A <br>T A H I R<br>R U I N E D<br>M E.</b><br><br><b>Side effects if reading ATATN:</b> dizziness, fatigue, lightheadedness, clammy skin, cold sweat, <i>P A I N.</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468921972ra/19758523.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>If you’ve read any of my updates, you’d know how <i>terrified</i> I was going into this- that I was expecting the worst.. and now I’m just sorry that I even doubted Sabaa Tahir. Because<b> absolutely every part of this book was brutal</b>, but also <i>perfection</i>. <br><br>All the best parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> were still a part of this story; the <i>complexity </i>of each and every character, the morals that are constantly questioned, and <b>the raw human emotion that is at the center of everything</b>. All those scenes where you’re silently <i>begging</i> for them to make it out of a terrifying situation, or *small moments of joy*- they’re all there. <br><br><b>
  <i>And also so much more.</i>
</b><br><br>After Elias and Laia run off in the last book, they encounter<b> their newest journey</b>.. to free Darin, Laia’s brother, from prison in order to help the Scholars have a fighting chance against the Empire. <br><br><b>Me at first page:</b> okay, that seems like it won’t be too bad<br><br><b>Me 60 pages in: </b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470032525ra/19880570.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you thought the first book was brutal.. <i>
  <b>this one is a million times worse</b>
</i>. I felt like the first book talked about and promised a lot of horrors, <b>but in this one it all comes to life.</b> <i>It is war</i> and everyone is fighting for their own, and there are no rules or limits as to how they do it. Everyone is fighting dirty, and it is absolutely terrifying.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>This is a mission.<br>You’re it’s leader.<br>This is the cost.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Like, the last book. I couldn’t get enough. I physically had to<i> FORCE</i> myself to take breaks and not devour it in an day. This isn’t like other books, because you honestly don’t know who will make it. <b>And not everyone does.</b> From the first page until the last page, I had non-stop anxiety for these characters.<br><br>This book is told from the same perspectives as the 1st, Laia and Elias’, but since they’re off on their own journey,<b> we also have Helene’s perspective </b>to let us see into the Empire. While Laia and Elias attempt to reach her brother's prison (and then somehow try and enter it), Helene is given the the task of finding &amp; executing Elias. <br><br><b>Aka everything is a mess.</b><br><br>I wish I could go into the romance (<i>and maybe I will once this comes out</i>), <u>but it would spoil pretty much everything</u>. Though, I can happily say that my ship is sort of happening, so there’s that! <b>Lots of twists and turns</b>, and wrong decisions happened, <i>which people may not like</i>.. but I understood. In the end, however, I think most people will be happy with everything.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You want to talk now? After weeks of not even looking at me?”<br>“I look at you.” His response is swift, his voice low. “Even when I shouldn’t.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Overall? <b>Sabaa killed it.</b> And I still can't wrap my brain around how she has created such an original, fast-paced, entertaining masterpiece <i>AND THEN TOPPED IT WITH THIS. </i>There were so many little details in the first book <b>that were finally explained</b> in this one, and <u>some shocking twists and turns that I doubt anyone will expect</u>. I highly recommend starting this series, I really can't compare it to much else because of how perfect it is. I really hope we get to see more of Laia and Elias, I feel so deeply connected to them at this point that <b>I can't think of this as being the end of their story.</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You are a torch against the night- if you dare to let yourself burn.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>Note:</b> There is apparently more books to come in this series! While this ending wouldn't be considered a cliffhanger, in my opinion, <b>there are many unanswered questions</b>. I think it's set up to be continued, so hopefully Tahir does that :D<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>And a huge thank you to Penguin Teen for giving me the opportunity to read this early :)</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>------<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6475890118942487496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1395839806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395839806" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395839806?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1395839806&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395839806" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16376849253512707538">This review will be more of a rant, don't say I didn't warn you.<br/><br/>I'm reviewing An Ember in the Ashes and a Torch Against the Night together in this review, mostly because I didn't have the energy to rant twice.<br/><br/>Because I don't like using acronyms, and typing out the titles taking long, we will refer to them as book 1 and 2. In book 1, we dive into a world with so many undeveloped yet interesting ideas. From the hype that surrounded this book, I was super excited to read it, and when it started off</span>
  <span id="freeText16376849253512707538" style="display:none">This review will be more of a rant, don't say I didn't warn you.<br /><br />I'm reviewing An Ember in the Ashes and a Torch Against the Night together in this review, mostly because I didn't have the energy to rant twice.<br /><br />Because I don't like using acronyms, and typing out the titles taking long, we will refer to them as book 1 and 2. In book 1, we dive into a world with so many undeveloped yet interesting ideas. From the hype that surrounded this book, I was super excited to read it, and when it started off with action, I thought oh yay this is going to be one of those fast paced excellent books! Man was I WRONG! First off, while the book tip toes around a pace that is sensible for the setting and action dwelling, it slows the scenes to a unbearable pace by contemplating every single characters emotions for what feels like a eternity. Let's start with the character Laia, shall we? We start by being introduced to her and her brother sneaking back into the house, and then the book plunges us into chaos. This would have been the perfect beginning, but laia's ineptness goes a long way to ruin it. One would wonder, how could an opinion be tarnished so early into a book? The answer is; make the main character whimpering and cowardly. My greatest complaint quite frankly is the superficiality of all the characters in this book. My personal adoration for this genre are kick ass female characters that overcome their worst fears. Laia is nothing even close, and I kept waiting for her to develop a spine, but even when the author was trying to portray her development I found I didn't like or even connect with her on any level. <br /><br />Moving on, I think I made my point. DID NOT LIKE THE MAIN CHARACTER ONE BIT. Now that that's settled, let's move on to the dynamics shall we? <br /><br />You seen my disappointment runs bone deep, because usually with books that provide a certain amount of Sanskrit influence, I'm pulled right in. It's the connection one makes with their own cultural ancestry. So all the more painful when I felt the great potential that this book had was wasted. Elias was no help either. A morally conflicted 20 something year old sucked into a life that was not his choosing seems like a good start for a character, add a touch of family problems and loyal best friends and you have a he perfect combination. But then he had to go all head over heals for a girl he just met, and ruin it all. <br /><br />When I say superficial, it's not just that people keep falling for each other, it's just that they fall, move on, fall again, and cycle again. I mean Keenan hated your guts then pledged his all undying love for you two second later and that didn't surprise you one bit? Even better, while mooning over him you start becoming infatuated with the son of the Enemy? All the while whining about how tough life is? Really? <br /><br />I think being quite honest, minus the characters, this book had a very red rising, hunger games, and Red queen with a touch of ancient Persia mixed with the Roman Empire. It was quite compelling and interesting, even the side characters were interesting enough, just not the ones the book revolves around. I mean even their mourning was superficial. You watch your grandparents get hacked to pieces and your only living relative in chains and your first thought is that you are a coward? This isn't about you! God! <br />Being honest the only character that had an influential role that I didn't absolutely hate was Helene. She was the only character with any semblance of a spine. She's probably the only reason I read the second book. Which took an eternity to get through. My disinterest was diminished for the last fifty pages of book two. But I literally had to read two whole books to get to a good last 50 pages, which doesn't soften the blow much. <br />Overall I don't think I will continue this series, even though so many people seems to love it, I was most definitely not one of them. Perhaps it was going in with such high expectations that shattered this book for me. Either way, not a memorable book for 2017,</span>
  <a data-text-id="16376849253512707538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1753469431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753469431" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753469431?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753469431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14096689858349030453">To keep up with the times, and not fall into a dark chasm of old school fantasy, nineteenth century literature, Buddhist philosophy and postcolonial theory, I make sure I read one popular Y.A book a year. I mean I’ve got to keep my cool trendy hip image going right? I wouldn’t want you guys to think I’m some kind of reclusive romantic poetry obsessed bookworm who sits around reading books all day then writes about them on a book review website. Cool, I’m glad we’ve cleared that up. <br/><br/>So I did have</span>
  <span id="freeText14096689858349030453" style="display:none">To keep up with the times, and not fall into a dark chasm of old school fantasy, nineteenth century literature, Buddhist philosophy and postcolonial theory, I make sure I read one popular Y.A book a year. I mean I’ve got to keep my cool trendy hip image going right? I wouldn’t want you guys to think I’m some kind of reclusive romantic poetry obsessed bookworm who sits around reading books all day then writes about them on a book review website. Cool, I’m glad we’ve cleared that up. <br /><br />So I did have fairly high expectations going into this one. The first book in the series was very good, and although it did replicate many of the tropes we keep seeing across the young adult genre, it did have a fair bit of originality. The world was based on Ancient Rome reworked with some fantasy elements. I liked it. It had a solid definition before the plot began. This one began in a very different way. It was much faster, for one, but that’s not always a good thing: it felt like plot had been sacrificed for action. <br /><br />A good chunk of the book is a perusal. Granted, the protagonists did escape a rather messy situation last time round, but the chase dragged on for far longer than I wanted it to. At one point I actually put the book down and considered if it was going anywhere in particular. The idea of the poison was just lame. It seemed like the author had included it to prevent Elias from being such a successful killing machine, that way there was a change of him being capture or even killed. I really didn’t like it. <br /><br /><b>So what did I like?</b><br /><br />Not much. Well the inclusion of a Helene point of view was great. It made the story remotely interesting. It broke up the terrible switching of point of views between Elias and Laia. Last time round it didn’t matter when they switched; their stories were in different places, but when two people who are travelling together swap back and forth it becomes slightly redundant. The romance became annoying, too blatant, and tiring. By the end I found myself rooting for “the bad guy” just so I could finish with this story and see no more of this nauseating so called “love” the characters thought they had for each other. <br /><br />Perhaps it’s me? Perhaps I’ve gone beyond a reading stage where I read books like this. I’ve always had an eclectic taste. I can enjoy a children’s book as much as I’d enjoy a highbrow piece of writing. But this just felt cheap. It took me almost two months to get through and it felt like an absolute slog. I won’t be bothering with the third book. I think I may just return to my chasm now. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14096689858349030453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1465135294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1465135294" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1465135294?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1465135294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5155045003112029690"><b>I’m deeply, truly underwhelmed. </b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_' title='An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Ember in the Ashes</a><b> is one of my favorite YA fantasy debuts</b>; <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir' title='Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sabaa Tahir</a>’s world was mesmerizing yet brutal, and it was so easy to lose myself in the bloody story of an Empire inspired by Greek and Roman culture. Sadly, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_' title='A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Torch Against the Night</a> I didn’t manage to fully grasp that flare of magic I was confident I’d find. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445993636ra/16730873.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So long as you fight the darkness, you stand in the light.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_' title='A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Torch Against the Night</a> follows Elias and Laia’s quest to free L</span>
  <span id="freeText5155045003112029690" style="display:none"><b>I’m deeply, truly underwhelmed. </b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a><b> is one of my favorite YA fantasy debuts</b>; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir" title="Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabaa Tahir</a>’s world was mesmerizing yet brutal, and it was so easy to lose myself in the bloody story of an Empire inspired by Greek and Roman culture. Sadly, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> I didn’t manage to fully grasp that flare of magic I was confident I’d find. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445993636ra/16730873.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So long as you fight the darkness, you stand in the light.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> follows Elias and Laia’s quest to free Laia’s brother from the Kauf prison, and Helene’s struggle to serve a loathsome Emperor and be the Blood Shrike everybody fears. <b>Their paths are intertwined, their feelings tangled, their loyalties divided. </b>Elias faces the cost of freedom, Laia the burden of crucial decisions, Helene the devastating choice between her best friend and her family, her duty, her honor. Ancient demons shadow their steps; the genocide of the Scholars drowns the streets in blood; a mad emperor’s reign of terror stifles every opposing voice; and an overly ambitious Commandant, a mother without love, a soldier serving a dark force, wreaks havoc, tortures and murders for her own agenda. In the Martial Empire, darkness prevails. But somewhere, between hopelessness and frustration, there's a torch against the night, which may be the guide to light. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are a torch against the night – if you dare let yourself burn.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>There is no doubt that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7770873.Sabaa_Tahir" title="Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabaa Tahir</a>’s pen is <b>exquisite</b>. The world she built is rich, full of Asian based lore, creatures of immense power and ruthless games. I can’t help but repeat that she succeeds in <b>combining beautiful moments and sentiments with savage murders, raw brutality, loss of innocence and despair</b>. As Laia and Elias traveled though the Martial Empire, with Helene high on their heels, we explored cultures, magical beings, heartache, and a major, jaw dropping plot twist that made the wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30809786.A_Reaper_at_the_Gates__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___3_" title="A Reaper at the Gates (An Ember in the Ashes, #3) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Reaper at the Gates</a> almost unbearable. <br><br><b>Helene’s chapters were my favorite part of the second instalment of this series.</b> Her inner battle, and her eventual, foretold breaking made her a character that shattered your heart, piece by piece. Sometimes I cringed at her choices, but given the circumstances, and what she would lose if she failed the horrible emperor she served, I couldn’t help but sympathize with her. Her storyline was laced with <b>politics, bloodshed and mistrust</b>, and the horrors she witnessed forged her into a mighty weapon to shatter her enemies. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Your emotions make you human. Even the unpleasant ones have a purpose. Don’t lock them away. If you ignore them, they just get louder and angrier.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Well in this context, I have to get it out of my system before it festers. I hate love triangles. I hate insta-love. And most of all, I hate <i>
  <b>instalovetriangles</b>
</i>. They are a plague that makes good stories turn sour, and characters you once respected insufferable. While the instalovetriangle was present in the previous book, it didn’t bother me that much because I was certain Laia and Elias were made for each other. In this one, though, I rolled my eyes so many times they still hurt. <i>Laia is so precious, Laia is so brave, Laia is such a special snowflake we should worship the ground her holy feet touch </i> oh my God just stop it already! I didn’t find anything special about her. She was a girl that tried to deal with all those things that went wrong in her life by lusting over every good looking guy she encountered. She forgot how Keenan belittled her or suffocated her because he was so <i>warm and familiar</i> and I couldn’t help but shout <b>YOU DON’T EVEN KNOW HIM DARN IT, GET OVER HIS WARMTH</b>! Who she loved depended on who was physically closer, that thing called brain didn’t function with all those hormones throwing a disco party! And Elias my love had fallen under her spell. I rooted for them, part of me still does, but Laia’s stupidity somehow tainted what I thought was pure. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525439583ra/25480496.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moreover, the fact that the majority of Elias and Laia’s arc took place on the road was rather tedious. I wanted something more, something I can’t put my finger on, but the magic of the first book, <b>the glorious radiance that made An Ember in the Ashes shimmer and sparkle and burn was not there. There was only a shadow of its potential. </b><br><br>Notwithstanding the above, <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25558608.A_Torch_Against_the_Night__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___2_" title="A Torch Against the Night (An Ember in the Ashes, #2) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Torch Against the Night</a> was an engaging story featuring diverse characters and war</b>, where civilizations collided and villains had the upper hand, ravaging and destroying. I just hope that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30809786.A_Reaper_at_the_Gates__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___3_" title="A Reaper at the Gates (An Ember in the Ashes, #3) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">A Reaper at the Gates</a> will meet the standards of the first book, and resurrect my somehow shaken faith in these characters and their respective quests! <br><br><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/1174-atorchagainstthenight" rel="nofollow noopener">Review also posted on BookNest!</a><br><br><b>
  <u>BEFORE</u>
</b><br><br>Guys guys GUYS WE HAVE A COVER!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444767573ra/16549263.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Elias baby, I've been waiting for you<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411285ra/807518.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5155045003112029690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12748238158950888521">is it possible to be simultaneously infuriated AND absolutely enamoured with a book? because im stuck in a constant struggle between wanting to throw this book across the room and clinging onto it for dear life. its making me begin to feel very emotionally unstable. <br/><br/>just to give you an idea, heres a basic summary of my reactions whilst reading this book:<br/><br/><blockquote>*laia does something*<br/> me: ughhhhh. you stupid, stupid girl. c’mon, get it together - im rooting for you!<br/><br/> *elias does something*<br/> me: noooooo. i c</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12748238158950888521" style="display:none">is it possible to be simultaneously infuriated AND absolutely enamoured with a book? because im stuck in a constant struggle between wanting to throw this book across the room and clinging onto it for dear life. its making me begin to feel very emotionally unstable. <br /><br />just to give you an idea, heres a basic summary of my reactions whilst reading this book:<br /><br /><blockquote>*laia does something*<br /> me: ughhhhh. you stupid, stupid girl. c’mon, get it together - im rooting for you!<br /><br /> *elias does something*<br /> me: noooooo. i cant believe youve done this!! whyyyyy!?!? but i still love you anyways, babe. ;) <br /><br /> *helene does something*<br /> me: disappointed, but not really surprised. (rolls eyes but secretly thinks about how savage she is)</blockquote><br />as you can see, the characters aggravate me off beyond belief in this book. but gosh, i would be lying if i said i didnt enjoy it. because this book is such a wild ride. it has the perfect balance of action and adventure (most of which stressed me out), with also enough teasing/hinting at things yet to come (so much so that ive turned into a crazy conspiracy theorist). <br /><br />i am just so in awe at the level of depth and the amount of various layers there are in this book/series. i know for sure this will be a re-read for me down the line because im positive there are so many things i have missed this first time around. so even if i disapprove of many things the characters did in this book, i am just so fully invested in them at this point that there is no turning back now. on to book three!!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>
